## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / solid mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in materials science. Stress typically depends on strain through elastic/plastic laws and on temperature through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed temperature)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (elastic-plastic with power-law hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (hardening with exponential temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law for pre-strained materials)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (thermally activated deformation, Garofalo-type)
- Temperature-dependent Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of flow stress → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**m) applied to strain-dependent terms
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), or Voce-type forms
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with n typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals
- Separable strain-temperature dependence → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T) suggesting independent mechanisms
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T) factors multiplying mechanical response
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c*epsilon**n) capturing both regimes
- Negative temperature sensitivity → Stress decreasing with temperature implies subtractive or decaying T-dependence
- Polynomial temperature dependence of modulus → E(T) = c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2 reflecting lattice thermal expansion effects
